asked the Minister of Agriculture, Irrigation and MahaweliDevelopment and Minister of Environment:(a) Will he inform this House,—

(i) whether the G.S.M.B. (Pvt.) Ltd. has beenestablished using four million rupees out of thecapital of the Geological Survey and MinesBureau;

(ii) when it was established;

(iii) the reasons for establishing the said institute;and

(iv) how approval was obtained for it?

(b) Is he aware that,—

(i) this company functions using funds andresources belonging to the said Bureau andmisusing public funds; and

(ii) the information pertaining to the contentiousissue has been provided to the Auditor-General?

(c) Will he accept that by the establishment of a privatecompany under the Geological Survey and MinesBureau, a loss is caused to the Bureau?

(d) If not, why?

asked the Minister of Education,:(a) Is he aware that—

(i) there are constant complaints from parents to theeffect that scholarship allowances due to studentswho have passed the year five ScholarshipExamination are not given in time;

(ii) such scholarship allowances have not beenreceived by some schools in the Ratnapura areafor a considerable period of time.(iii) this drawback prevails in schools in the otherareas of the island as well?

(b) Will he admit that—

(i) since most of these scholarship holders arestudents of poor, rural families, their parents faceimmense difficulties as they do not receive themoneys expected;

(ii) due to this very reason, the principals of thoseschools concerned face much inconvenience?

(c) Will he inform this House of the action that will betaken in this regard?

(d) If not, why?

.asked the Minister of Industrial Development:(a) Is he aware that 24 trainees belonging to the Clericaland Allied grades have undergone training at theColombo Head Office of Sri Lanka Mineral SandsLimited and the Pulmudai Service Station upto13.11.2005?

(b) Will he inform this House of the names andaddresses of the said Trainees?

(c) Will he state—

(i) at whose request these trainees had been enlistedfor training;

(ii) the basis on which this was done;

(iii) whether these trainees have been provided withpermanent appointments;

(iv) if so, when the interviews were conducted;

(v) Since when the permanent appointments havebeen given; and

(vi) the date from which these appointments beeffective?

(d) If not, why?

asked the Minister of Education:(a) Will he state this House—

(i) the names of all the Tamil Medium Schools inthe island and the number of male and femalestudents in each of such schools separately;

(ii) separately, according to classes the number ofteachers who teach in those schools;

(iii) the subjects taught by them;

(iv) the number of teachers who should have beenon the staff of those schools;

(v) the subjects for which there is a shortage ofteachers; and

(vi) the hours of commencement and closure of theseschools?

(b) Will he take steps to submit to the House thereports of the principals and zonal Directors ofeducation with regard to all those particulars?

(c) Will he take steps to obtain separate writtensubmissions from the principals with regard to thedevelopments that need to be done in respect ofeach school and submit them to the House?

(d) If not, why?

asked the Minister of Urban Development and Water Supply:(a) Will he inform this House—

(i) the extent of land earmarked to be granted to theformer President from the Madiwela area;

(ii) which institution owns this particular land;

(iii) the value per perch as assessed by theGovernment Assessor and the market value perperch of the said land that has been so set asidefor that purpose;

(iv) the total market value of the said land?

(b) Will he state the conditions under which it will begiven, if this plot of land is to be given in keepingwith the criteria of the Urban Development Authority?

(c) If not, why?

asked the Minister of Disaster Management and HumanRights:(a) Will he inform this House of—

(i) the number of houses destroyed in Sri Lanka dueto the tsunami disaster on 26.12.2004; and

(ii) the number of houses built by the Governmentand NGOs separately, to replace the destroyedbuildings?

(b) Will he state this house—

(i) out of those, how many houses have been builtunder the patronage of the local and foreignmonks; and

(ii) the names of the monks and the relevantorganizations that extended their support?

(i) the number of houses built under the patronageof the other clergy of religions?

(ii) the number of houses that is left to be built; and

(iii) when these houses be built?

(d) If not why?

asked the Prime Minister and Minister of InternalAdministration and Deputy Minister of Defence:(a) Will he inform this House the number of variouscomplaints received by the Madegama PoliceStation in the Moneragala District from 01.05.2005to 08.05.2006?

(b) Will he state separately,—

(i) out of the said complaints, the number ofelection complaints received during the electionperiod;

(ii) the number of complaints inquired into andadjudicated;

(iii) the number of complaints which have not beeninquired into?

(c) Will he state separately, the number of complaintswhich have not been inquired into and the numberof complaints which were not election related andyet have been inquired into and adjudicated?

(d) Will he submit to this house separately, in respectof each complaint received,—

(i) the dates on which the uninquired complaintswere received and the names of the officers whorecorded those complaints;

(ii) the nature of the complaints and the reason fornot inquiring into it?

(e) Will he state the measures that will be taken fornot inquiring into the said complaints?

(f) If not, why?

asked the Prime Minister and Minister of InternalAdministration and Deputy Minister of Defence:(a) Will he inform this House the number of variouscomplaints received by the Madulla Police Stationin the Moneragala District from 01.05.2005 to08.05.2006?

(b) Will he state separately,—

(i) out of the said complaints, the number of electioncomplaints received during the election period;

(ii) the number of complaints inquired into andadjudicated;

(iii) the number of complaints which have not beeninquired into?

(c) Will he state separately, the number of complaintswhich have not been inquired into and the numberof complaints which were not election related andyet have been inquired into and adjudicated?

(d) Will he submit to this house separately, in respectof each complaint received,—

(i) the dates on which the uninquired complaintswere received and the names of the officers whorecorded those complaints;

(ii) the nature of the complaints and the reason fornot inquiring into it?

(e) Will he state the measures that will be taken for notinquiring into the said complaints?

(f) If not, why?

2006 °ìÈè 2132053206

¨»å¾åÆ¨ºëÄå(±¹Ç·Ç»¯¼Æ £Á¼Æ¯¿Æ)(Mr. Speaker)ïÂåïÍåÄ ÌàºíºøÆú. ªÇæ ï¼àÊ ¨´Æêºë ¡ÄåºñºëÄå.

ïÈÂ¾¾ïÆà Ìè¾ Êòé Èåâ¨ø¨Æ¾à´ÌÍÆÑÄ : ªÇæ ï¼àÊ ¨´Æêºë ¡Äåºñ ÌÍ ÉÇåÆÍå ªëÉ¾à ïÌàÉå ¡ÄåºñºëÄåïªà Àò¨åÊÆÌ¾¹¸Ç¸È¾Æ §¿Æ¿ ¥¾+ÆÎ¯»¼Æ¯à¯ÆÐ §¶â¶¾Æ :ÌÁ¿È·Ç´Æ´ßÁ¾Æ¯¿Æ £Îº±Æ±ÝºÆ ×Î½Û¯+Æ¯¿Æ,ºÇ¸ Í±ÎÁ¯¿Æ £Îº±Æ±ÝºÇ¸Á¼× ç½ÆÞASSISTANCE TO SRI LANKANS IN LEBANON :STATEMENT BY MINISTER OF FOREIGN AFFAIRS ANDMINISTER OF PORTS AND AVIATION

ªÇæ ÄâªÈ ÌÄÇÑÇ ÄÍºå (ï¼àÊ ¨´Æêºë ¡Äåºñ ÌÍ ÉÇåÆ ÍåªëÉ¾à ïÌàÉå ¡ÄåºñºëÄå)(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ º+Æ¯¿ ±º¼¼ - ÌÁ¿È·Ç´Æ´ßÁ¾Æ¯¿Æ £Îº±Æ±ÝºÆ×Î½Û¯+Æ¯¿Æ, ºÇ¸±Æ Í±ÎÁ¯¿Æ £Îº±Æ±ÝºÆ)(The Hon. Mangala Samaraweera - Minister of Foreign Affairsand Minister of Ports and Aviation)Thank you Mr. Speaker for allowing me to make thisstatement on a matter of great national importance. As youknow Mr. Speaker since the breakout of hostilities in Lebanonlast week, the Ministry of Foreign Afairs, together with ourEmbassy in Lebanon has taken a wide range of measures toprovide emergency assistance to Sri Lankans in areas affectedby the ongoing attacks in that country. There areapproximately, according to reports, 80,000 Sri Lankanscurrently in Lebanon, and the majority are unskilled workers.

The Sri Lankan Embassy in Beirut, since the hostilitiesbroke out a week ago, has set up a 24 hour information deskwhere Sri Lankans can call and seek assistance. Similartelephone inquiry facilities have been set up at the ConsularAffairs Division of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Colombowhere Sri Lankans concerned about their family members orrelatives in Bebanon can call for information. I understandthat the SLBFE, that is the Sri Lanka Bureau of ForeignEmployment, has also set up similar facilities. All thesenumbers have already been given publicity through the mediahere in Sri Lanka.

As of Wednesday, Mr. Speaker, approximately 200 SriLankans have sought shelter at the Embassy. They are beingaccommodated and provided with the essential facilitiesincluding food, basis healthcare and local transport at centresrun with the assistance of CARITAS.

In addition, the Embassy has already held discussions withthe local authorities in Beirut and humanitarian agencies suchas CARITAS and IOM with regard to additional safe sheltersin places of religious worship, that could be used, should thenumbers seeking shelter increase. We have also haddiscussions to repatriate Sri Lankans who wish to leave Beirutand let me take this opportunity to thank IOM and CARITASfor their support and co-operation.

The Embassy in Beirut has also been strengthened withadditional local staff; two SLBFE officials and one ForeignMinistry officer to handle inquiries and help Sri Lankansseeking assistance.

The Ministry is working in close co-ordination with theMinistry of Labour, the SLBFE and our Embassies in theregion. Additional funds of Rs. 2.5 million have been allocatedfrom the SLBFE for food, temporary shelter, health, localtransportet cetera for the affected Sri Lankans.

I regret to inform that one confirmed death has beenreported so far of a Sri Lankan national. Details of the next ofkin are awaited to make further arrangements. Our Embassyis working with the Sri Lankan community to ascertain furtherdetails regarding others who may be vulnerable in affectedlocalities.

Steps are also being taken Mr. Speaker, to repatriate SriLankans who have expressed a wish to leave the countryacross the border of Damascus, Syria by bus. Many of themhave arrived in Damascus already and this morning a SriLankan Airlines plane will leave for Damascus to airlift thesepeople back to Colombo.

In fact, we have made arrangements to dispatch a SriLankan Airlines aircraft and during the course of the day, Ibelieve at 11.30 a.m. this morning an A330 Airbus will fly toDamascus and bring back the first batch of Sri Lankansnumbering about 300.

Let me also take this opportunity to thank the Chairmanand the CEO of Sri Lankan Airlines for extending theirassistance to our countrymen in Beirut in their hour of need.Foreign governments concerned have also been contactedwith regard to assisting a possible large-scale evacuation ofSri Lankans out of Lebanon, particularly with regard to safepassage and provision of ships should the need arise.

In fact my Ministry has been in touch with the Governmentof India, the Government of United States of America, theGovernment of Italy and the Government of Turkey on thepossibility of naval evacuations of Sri Lankans from Beirut ifthe need arises. In fact the Government of Israel has alsoassured us of safe passage for vessels carrying Sri Lankansdespite the naval blockade.

The Government of Sri Lanka has expressed the hope thatthe parties involved in hostilities would ease the situationand work towards a cessation of attacks and counter attacks.We have also expressed support to the United Nations andothe regional efforts for bringing about a cessation of violenceand the resolution of issues at hand.

Thank you.

ÄÄ ÊàÉåÌ¨Ç¾àï¾à ¾æÍæ, ¦à¨´ §ÂºëÄå ¦¨­ ïÉÆú ¨øÆÈå. ¦à ¾øÌå ïÄå¾ À¨àËïÆàÉê¸ºà, ïÄå¾ ¨¸à¶åÆï Éê¸ºà ¦à «åº¾ ÌÂ¾à½É ï°åàÊÀà ÀÇÇå°ÌèâÍÄæºøºëÄå ïÇåà½ºåïÉ¾à ¡¨Äæºàïº¾à ÍúÆå. ¦ºëÄå ÀòåÚ»¾å ¨ïÈà ¦ºëÄåïªà¡åªÄ ¼ÍÄ ¡¾êÉ ¦ºëÄå Àæºëï ÌàÉÚªÆ´ Æ¾à¾Æú. ¾ºàºÈà ¼ÉÌ Éæ¾ø ¡ºø¤¡ºë ¼ÉÌ¨ ¦à Ìèó ÑèÄ ªæ¾ ¨¾ªå´ê É¾ ¡ºÇ ¦ºëÄå Àæºí ¡å¨åÇÆ´¦ºëÄå´ ÌàÉÚªÆ´ Æ¾à¾ ÉÇ ÈæïÉå, ¦à Éåïªà Ä Äïªà ¡åªï ÍæÆ´¦ºëÄå´ ¾øÉ¾à ÌêÉ ¡ºà ïÉå ¨øÆå ÀòåÚ»¾å ¨Ç¾à ïÄå¾ÇåªÈ ¼úÌàºòè¨à¨ïÆà°¾ºåÉïªà ïÊåà¨Æºà Äïªà ïÀð¼àªÈè¨ ïÊåà¨Æºà ¦ºëÄåïªà ÀÉêïÈà ÌèÆõï¼¾å´ ¼¾àÉå ÆÉ¾ ïÈÌ ¢ÈàÈå Ìè¾à ÄÄ ¾øÍ¹ ïÉ¾Éå. ïÂåïÍåÄÌàºíºøÆú.

ªÇæ È¨àËàÄ¾à ¨øÖ¡æÈàÈ ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ¾¯Æº ¯È¼È©¾Æ¾)(The Hon. Lakshman Kiriella)Hon. Presding Member, I wish to associate myself with thesentiments of the House.

I remember meeting the Hon. Joseph Pararajasingham in1990. I entered Parliament in 1989 and, I think after the deathof the Hon. Sam Tambimuttu the Hon. Pararajasinghamenered Parliament.

the Hon. Joseph Pararajasingham was a tamil leader, whowas a moderate. I had the good fortune of attending severalconferences abroad with the hon. Pararajasingham. He was amoderate Tamil leader and the remarkable thing about himwas that he believed in a united Sri Lanka.

Mr. Presiding Member, you may also agree with the viewthat since Independence, the mistake made by all Governmentswas that we never negotiated with the moderate Tamil leaderswho were in Parliament from 1948. We had very educationed,decent and important Tamil Members of Parliament afterIndependence. They were lawyers; they were businessmen.They did not ask for a separate Sstate. They only asked fortheir language rights. I remember, in 1956 They asked fortheir language rights. they wanted their cultural identitypreserved. They never wanted a separate State. Even as lateas 1980, they asked for District Development Councils. TheHon. amirthalingam was satisfied with he DistrictDevelopment Councils. But, unfortunately, all Governmentsignored the moderate leaders. ¡Àè §¨àï¨åÄ Ä½ñÌà» ¾åÆ¨Æ¾à¡Äº¨ ¨Îå. ¦à ¡Äº¨ ¨ø×èÄ ¾øÌå ÆåÀ¾Æ Àòï¼àÊÆ ¡¾àºÉå¼û¾à´ ¡ÆºàÉê¸å. Therefore, Mr. Presiding Member, it is still not too lateeven now. In the present Parliament, there are moderate TamilLeaders who wish to negotiate for a united Sri Lanka, toshare power and I hope the death of the Hon. JosephPararajasingham will be a catalyst in that direction.

Then, Sir with regard to his unfortunate death, it happenedon Christmas Day. Adding insult to injury, it happened insidea church. The entire international community was reallyalarmed at these unfortunate developments in the Easternpart of Sri Lanka on Christmas Day.

Sir, I might also mention that since we entered Parliamentin 1989, several Sinhala and Tamil Members of Parliamenthave been assassinated in this marner. But, unfortunately, wehave not been able to track a single person involved in thesekillings. We have had Tamil leaders killed, Sinhala leaderskilled, but the law enforcement authorities have failed toprosecute a single person involved in these incidents. I think,it is really an indictment on the law enforcement authoritiesof Sri lanka.

So therefore, Mr. Presiding Member, it is high time thatMembers on both sides of the House get together. It is stillnot too late. Even in this Parliament, there are Tamil Membersof Parliament who speak to us privately. They want a solution.They are not for terrorist activities. They do not support thiskind of activity. They are for peace; they are for sharing ofpower. I must say that the United National Party beliecesthat, whilst safeguarding the rights of the Sinhala majority,the Buddhist majority, we must also safeguard the rights ofthe Muslims and the Tamils living in Sri Lanka. Because,whether you like it or not, 25 per cent of this country consistof Muslims, Tamils, Christians and Hindus and if we are tobuild a united Sri Lanka, we must safeguard their rights. Asfar as the United National Party is concerned, we will supportthe measures of the Government. Our Leader, the Hon. RanilWickremasinghe, has always been consistent. He did not sayone thing during the election time, another thing before theelection and yet another thing after the election. He alwayssaid, “I am for a United Sri Lanka.” If the persent Governmentfollows the Olso accord to share power under a federalsolution, we will support the measures of the Government.

So, I think, the biggest tribute one could pay to the Hon.Joseph Pararajasingham is to make this country a unitedcountry, not a divided country and I hope the Governmentwould accept the support given by the UNP to achieve thatend.

Thank you.

Subscription : The annual subscription for Official Report of Hansard is Rs. 2,178. A single copy of Hansard is available forRs. 18.15. (Postage Rs. 2.50) Copies can be obtained by remitting in advance an annual subscription fee to theSUPERINTENDENT, GOVERNMENT PUBLICATION BUREAU, No. 32, Transworks House,Lotus Road, Colombo 1. The fee should reach him on or bvefore November 30 each year.Late application for subscriptions will not be accepted.
